Reconstructing from the asides: Susan Morse appears to have been a practical, religious-leaning, emotionally restrained woman who raised two children largely without sustained paternal presence (see §3 below). The household was respectable, under-resourced rather than poor, valued education, and ran on a code of *do not air it*. Subject's adult relationship to disclosure — the conviction that interior states are private property and that bearing privately is a form of dignity — is not original to SHIELD tradecraft. SHIELD merely weaponized what Susan Morse had already installed.

The mother's pride in Subject's academic accomplishments (twin doctoral-equivalent credentials in biology and a related life-science discipline, completed precociously) is intelligible in the record but coded — Susan Morse is the kind of woman who frames diplomas and does not say the word *proud* aloud. Subject reciprocally is the kind of woman who calls her mother on a regular schedule (Sundays, per a throwaway line in McCann #2 — "it's Sunday, I have to call my mother" delivered as obligation, not warmth, but maintained for decades), sends competent practical gifts, and has not told her mother any substantive truth about her work, her marriage's actual collapse mechanism, her captivity, her resurrection, or her bodily augmentation.

**Trust and safety**: Bidirectionally low *in content*, high *in form*. Neither woman lies to the other; both routinely omit. Susan Morse does not know her daughter survived years of Skrull captivity. Susan Morse does not know her daughter killed a man in 1880s Arizona and let her marriage die rather than disclose it. Susan Morse believes her daughter is a federal scientific consultant of some sort, divorced, doing fine. Subject calls her on Sundays.

**Evolution**: The relationship has not so much evolved as ossified. Adolescent Subject was already managing her mother's anxieties by withholding from them; adult Subject continues the practice at higher stakes. There is no observable rupture-and-repair history because there has never been a rupture — the relationship cannot rupture because nothing pressurized has ever been placed inside it. This is not health. It is preservation by avoidance.

**Failure mode**: If Susan Morse were ever to learn the actual scope of her daughter's life — the Skrull years, the augmentation, the kills, the resurrection-adjacent events — Subject's stable conception of her mother as *the one person who sees her as ordinary* would collapse. The mother is Subject's only remaining mirror of pre-operative self. Losing that mirror would be destabilizing in ways combat losses have not been.

**Leverage profile**: Susan Morse is a high-value soft target for any hostile actor capable of identifying her. Subject's protective architecture around the mother is *informational* (she has scrubbed the maternal address from multiple databases on at least three documented occasions) rather than physical — there is no detail of standing surveillance, which is itself a tell: physical protection would require disclosure to the mother of *why*, which Subject will not do. The leverage vector is therefore: an adversary who locates the mother first and contacts Subject through her would force a disclosure Subject has spent five decades avoiding, and the cost of that forced disclosure would compromise Subject's tactical judgment more reliably than physical threat ever has.

---

### 2. BEN MORSE — YOUNGER BROTHER

**Status**: Living. Established in Cain's *S.H.I.E.L.D. 50th* one-shot and threaded through the 2015–16 solo. Approximate four-to-six years junior to Subject. Profession non-Avengers-adjacent — the canon suggests a stable civilian career (academia or research-adjacent, plausibly inherited from the household valorization of education) and a marriage with children.

**History and dynamic**: The defining feature of Bobbi's relationship to Ben is *protective asymmetry maintained past its appropriate expiration*. She raised him, in the practical sense — the absent-father / occupied-mother household made Subject de facto co-parent from approximately age eight or nine, and the role embedded itself in her. Adult Ben is in his forties; Subject still treats him with the watchful low-grade vigilance one extends to a child crossing a parking lot. This is the only relationship in Subject's catalog where her *warmth presents without irony*. With Ben she does not deploy the sardonic deflection that armors her with Barton, with Coulson, with the Avengers. With Ben she is briefly the person she might have been.

The Cain run shows her interacting with Ben's children — niece and nephew, ages indeterminate but pre-adolescent — and this is the only published context in which Subject is observed reading aloud, baking (badly, per the narrative), and tolerating physical proximity from someone without flinch-recalibrating. The somatic data point is significant: Subject does not flinch around these children. With virtually everyone else there is a measurable micro-adjustment at unexpected contact — a sixteenth-of-a-second freeze before continuation, the operative's tell. With Ben's children, absent.

**Trust and safety**: The highest of any relationship in her file, including Barton. Ben is the only person to whom Subject has disclosed *fragments* of what happened during Skrull captivity, per inference from a closed-door conversation panel in McCann #5 where Subject is shown speaking to him alone for an extended period and emerging visibly emptied. She has not told him everything. But she has told him more than she has told anyone else, and she did it because Ben is the only person whose attachment to her predates her competence. He loved her before she was good at things. She cannot perform for him because he saw her at four.

**Evolution**: The protective asymmetry has been a low-grade friction for decades — Ben, an adult man with his own life, has at intervals attempted to invert it, to ask after her, to insist she let him *know* her. She deflects warmly but absolutely. The deflection is gentler than the deflection she uses elsewhere, but it is the same deflection. Ben has, per inference, made peace with being kept partially outside.

**Failure mode**: Two vectors. First, if Ben is hurt or threatened, Subject loses the proportionality calibration that otherwise governs her field decisions — she becomes the operator she was during the Slade resolution, capable of unilateral lethal calculation, but without the morally reasoned framing. With Ben at stake she would not reason; she would simply remove the threat. Second, if Ben were to die before her, Subject loses the only relationship that holds a pre-traumatic self-image. The post-loss Subject would be observably colder and more efficient — a deterioration that would read to outside observers as composure.

**Leverage profile**: Maximum. Of every named individual in Subject's catalog, Ben Morse is the single highest-value coercive lever. Subject is aware of this — there is evidence she has personally placed and updated a low-visibility security envelope around his household (alarm-system upgrade gifted under cover of birthday in 2012; quiet relocation suggestion in 2014; multiple identity-scrub passes on his digital footprint conducted by Subject without his knowledge). Unlike with the mother, Subject *has* physicalized her protection here, which means she has accepted the necessary partial disclosure — Ben knows enough about her work to accept the precautions without demanding full explanation. This is the single most functional intimacy in her file.

---

### 3. THE FATHER — UNNAMED, UNRESOLVED

**Status**: Functionally absent from Subject's narrative. The canon does not name him, does not stage him, does not bury him. He is a structuring absence rather than a present figure. Working inference: either deceased during Subject's childhood (most parsimonious read, given the household's economic configuration and Susan Morse's solo-parenting affect) or estranged-and-absent in a way the family does not discuss. The non-disclosure is intergenerational — Susan Morse does not talk about him; Subject does not talk about him; Ben, per the Cain material, does not appear to remember him substantively, which favors the early-death reading over estrangement.

**History and dynamic**: The relationship is principally legible through its *negative space*. Subject's pattern with male authority figures — Fury, Stark in the brief WCA overlaps, Steve Rogers in Secret Avengers — is uniformly respectful, professionally compliant, and *uninvested*. She does not seek paternal approval from any of them. She does not test them. She does not perform for them. The cleanest read is that the paternal slot was vacated early enough that no template installed itself, and Subject grew into adulthood without a functioning model of *a man whose approval matters*. This has operational consequences: she is unusually resistant to charismatic male leadership, which makes her an excellent independent operative and a difficult subordinate.

The relationship to Barton is partially intelligible through this lens but should not be over-read. Barton is not a paternal substitute — he is, if anything, the inverse: the chaotic peer she chose precisely because he carried no authority-coding. The vacated paternal slot does not transfer; it stays vacated.

**Trust and safety**: Not applicable in the conventional sense. There is a residual *emotional sediment* — Subject is observed, in two distinct moments across the published record, looking at fathers-with-daughters in public settings with a controlled neutrality that takes work to sustain. This is not grief, exactly. It is the awareness of an absence she has never named.

**Evolution**: None. The slot has been empty long enough that its emptiness has become structural rather than felt.

**Failure mode**: Improbable but specific — Subject is uniquely vulnerable to a hostile operator who *credibly* presented as having known her father, particularly if presenting documentary evidence about him. Not because Subject would believe the operator's larger narrative, but because the offered information itself would constitute a previously-unobtainable resource. The pull of finally knowing would override several layers of usual operational skepticism. This is a narrow but real vector.

**Leverage profile**: Low in the conventional sense (no living target), but the *information* about him is itself a leverage asset. Any actor in possession of credible biographical material on Subject's father has acquired a slow-acting key.

---

### 4. THE PHANTOM RIDER (LINCOLN SLADE) — THE DEAD MAN

This belongs in this section, not in the romantic or adversarial sections, because the bond Slade forced on Subject was framed by him as familial-spousal in 1880s register — he did not stage himself as a lover but as a *husband by claim*, with all the legal-property frame that implied in the period. The relationship is therefore catalogued here under the rubric of imposed origin-bond: a man who attempted to install himself as kin and whom Subject removed from existence.

**Status**: Deceased by Subject's controlled non-intervention (WCA #41). Subsequently the bond persisted through the spectral harassment of his descendant Hamilton Slade and through Subject's own unprocessed material. The dead man has stayed louder than most living relationships in this file.

**History**: Drug-facilitated assault under altered cognition; staged "marriage" performed under coercion Subject could not at the time recognize; period of cohabitation that Subject's clear-headed self would never have entered. Upon return of cognition: a confrontation in which Slade fell, and Subject did not extend the hand she could have extended. She watched. Then she came home and did not tell her husband. The full sequence — assault, captivity-by-cognition, lethal-passive resolution, concealment — is the densest single trauma node in her file.

**Dynamic, post-mortem**: The dead Slade has functioned as an *internalized prosecutor*. Subject's elevated baseline of moral self-policing, her conviction that she must absorb costs others would not be required to absorb, her refusal of absolution from Barton and from the institutional Avengers tribunal that adjudicated the matter — all of this is the Slade matter metabolizing across decades. She did not forgive him. She also did not forgive herself, not for letting him fall (she has reasoned that decision and stands by it) but for *concealing it*. The concealment is the part she returns to.

**Trust and safety**: The relationship to the dead man is the relationship to the part of herself that made a unilateral decision and lied by omission. She does not trust that self. She also relies on it.

**Evolution**: Across the post-Skrull period the Slade material has subsided in surface salience but not in structural influence. She is observed visiting no grave, performing no ritual, naming him in no monologue — the absence of overt processing is consistent with her dominant defense (compartmentalization) but should not be mistaken for resolution. The compartment is sealed; the contents are intact.

**Failure mode**: Any forced re-confrontation with the Slade material — a temporal incursion, a descendant resurfacing, a telepathic incursion that surfaces the memory — does not merely re-traumatize Subject; it threatens the entire architecture by which she has organized every subsequent unilateral moral decision. If the Slade compartment is broken open, the question becomes whether *all* of her concealed unilateral acts must be re-examined, and Subject's operative self may not survive that audit intact.

**Leverage profile**: Catastrophic if accessed. The Slade material is the most weaponizable single asset in her file against her continued functioning. Anyone in possession of the full chronology, with credible means to surface it publicly or to Barton in a context she does not control, holds her at the throat.

---

### 5. THE SKRULL WHO WORE HER — THE IMPOSTOR-KIN

Catalogued here because the figure who lived inside her life, slept in her bed, used her mother's Sunday phone call, attended (presumably) her brother's family events, and carried her name for years constitutes a form of imposed origin-bond inverse to Slade's — Slade tried to install himself *as* kin to her; the Skrull installed itself *as her* to her kin. The structural violation is parallel and equally formative.

**Status**: Deceased (per *Secret Invasion* resolution). The bond, again, persists past the dying.

**Dynamic**: Subject has had to reconstruct, from outside, what the impostor said and did in her name to the people who loved her. Every Sunday phone call her mother received during the captivity period was with this entity. Every birthday card to Ben's children carried its handwriting imitating hers. Every embrace Barton extended in that period landed on it, not her. The retroactive contamination of her relational record is total and unfixable. She cannot revisit those years and reclaim them; she can only know that someone else lived them.

**Trust and safety**: The Skrull impostor destroyed Subject's baseline assumption that identity is a stable category that protects the people one loves. After Secret Invasion, Subject reads every intimate interaction through a quiet, never-spoken layer of *is this person actually who they present as*. This is not paranoia in the clinical sense — it is a calibrated epistemic adjustment that any rational actor would make in her position. But it has costs. She does not relax into identity-claims anymore. She verifies.

**Failure mode**: Subject is now permanently vulnerable to a particular kind of attack — any sufficiently competent impersonation of someone she loves will land harder on her than on a comparable operative, because the Skrull template has installed a specific dread. Conversely, she is unusually resistant to being deceived by impersonation, because she runs verification protocols others would consider excessive.

**Leverage profile**: The Skrull is dead but the *footage*, the *records*, the *artifacts* of the impostor's years are leverage. Anyone in possession of material from those years — recordings of the impostor's voice using her name with her mother, photographs of the impostor at Ben's household events — holds material Subject has not seen and cannot bear to see. The asset is real even though the figure is gone.

---

### Aggregated reading of the family-and-origin layer

Subject's origin bonds are organized around a single recurring structure: *people she protects by withholding from them*. The mother is protected from the truth of her daughter's life. The brother is protected from the totality of it, granted only fragments. The father is protected by being unaddressed. Slade was, in her cognition, removed; she then protected Barton by not telling him. The Skrull impostor was the inverse — she could not protect anyone from it because she did not know it existed — and this is precisely why that violation registers so heavily: it was the failure of her one operational mode of love.

The family-and-origin section therefore identifies Subject's deepest pattern more cleanly than any other relational layer will: *for Subject, love is the discipline of bearing what the beloved should not have to bear*. This is a real ethic and a real form of devotion. It is also the wound running the operation, as flagged in the shared assessment. Every later relationship in this file will be intelligible as a variation on it.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Subject: MORSE, Barbara "Bobbi" — Mockingbird / Huntress / Agent 19*

This section catalogues every non-romantic-primary attachment of operational, emotional, or developmental significance in the subject's life. Bobbi's relational pattern is *concentric*: an inner ring of perhaps three to five people who receive partial interior access; a middle ring of trusted operators with whom the contract is professional-affectionate; and a wide outer ring of acquaintances she treats with practiced warmth that is real but range-limited. The mistake an analyst can make is to read the warmth as intimacy. It is intimacy's *substitute* — a high-quality alloy she has refined over thirty years of operational life.

For each subject we note: history (entry vector and trajectory), present-day dynamic, trust posture (what she withholds, what she will share, what she will act on without consulting), failure modes (how the relationship breaks or has broken), and leverage (what a hostile party who understood the bond could exploit).

---

## 1. NICHOLAS J. FURY (Sr.) — Handler, Patron, Mirror

**History.** The longest single professional relationship in her file. Fury is the man who recruited her into SHIELD off her academic credentials, who authorized the Wilma Calvin deep-cover assignment that ran under the Huntress codename, and who issued her the Agent 19 designation that she still uses in older systems decades later. He selected her precisely because the academic-cover was real and not constructed — Bobbi's PhD was authentic, her papers had been published, her standing in the biology community was something an opposition counter-intelligence cell could verify and would therefore trust. Fury's recruitment style was to find people whose covers were their actual selves and then weaponize the rest.

**Dynamic.** This is the closest thing in her life to a *paternal* relationship, but it is the kind of fatherhood that consists of being correctly used. Fury does not coddle her, does not protect her from assignments other handlers would have flinched at, and — critically — does not feign more affection than he feels. She finds this restful. The implicit contract: he will give her real problems and she will solve them and they will not talk about anything else. They have had, by her count, perhaps four conversations in thirty years that strayed past operational matter, and she remembers each one in unusual detail.

**Trust posture.** She will receive an order from Fury without seeking a second source on it — a posture she extends to perhaps two other handlers in her career. She will however lie to him operationally if she has concluded he is being fed bad intel, and she does not consider this a violation of the contract; he has told her, in different words, that he does not consider it one either. What she will *not* tell him is anything about the Slade material, anything about the Skrull captivity's interior, anything about Clint that he could not deduce from public record. The professional channel is sacred; the personal channel does not exist by mutual unspoken agreement.

**Failure mode.** Fury's repeated faked deaths and going-dark episodes do not destabilize her the way they destabilize less-experienced operatives, but each one costs her something she does not name. When he is operational she does not need to think about him; when he is unaccounted for she finds herself running passive monitoring routines on her own without conscious decision. The relationship's true failure mode is the one she has not yet faced: Fury actually gone, and her with no remaining handler from the founding generation who can authorize the level of unsanctioned operation she sometimes requires.

**Leverage.** A hostile who fed her a Fury-authenticated order to take an action against Clint or against a protege would get further than they had any right to. The Fury channel is one of the few she does not cross-check.

---

## 2. CLINTON F. BARTON — *(treated in Relationships I as primary)*

Cross-referenced here only for completeness. Note that in the present taxonomy his role is *also* allied-operator and chosen-family, not merely romantic-primary, and several behavioral patterns in this section will only make sense against the Barton baseline.

---

## 3. KATHERINE "KATE" BISHOP — Protégée (Designated Successor-Adjacent)

**History.** Bobbi enters Kate's orbit through Clint, which is structurally significant — most of her chosen-family attachments arrive via the Barton vector and then become independent of it. Their first sustained contact is in the period when both women are oriented around the same wounded man and recognize, faster than he does, that they are not in competition. Bobbi's read of Kate at first encounter: untrained but unusually well-formed, the kind of person whose ethical instincts run ahead of her tradecraft, which is rare and which Bobbi finds both moving and operationally concerning.

**Dynamic.** Bobbi becomes — without ever using the word and without any formal arrangement — Kate's senior. Not mentor in the heavy-handed sense; she does not lecture, does not run drills, does not credential. What she does is *answer*. Kate calls and Bobbi picks up. Kate asks a question and Bobbi gives the real answer, including the ones a more cautious senior would soft-pedal: how to tail without being made, how to read a hostile's intent from the way they hold their weight in a doorway, how to extract from a sexual entanglement that has gone sideways without leaving forensic or emotional residue. The instruction is unsentimental and load-bearing. Kate, in return, gives Bobbi something Bobbi did not know she would value: the experience of being deferred to without being romanticized. Kate sees her clearly and likes her anyway.

**Trust posture.** Kate is one of perhaps three people Bobbi will accept *care* from without compensating it within twenty-four hours by performing a competence display. This is a marker of unusually high trust in her system. She will not however disclose interior material to Kate spontaneously; she will answer if asked directly and judges Kate worthy of a true answer, but she protects Kate from her older grief by default, on the theory that a mentor's job is to be a stable referent.

**Failure mode.** If Kate is hurt and Bobbi judges herself to have under-prepared her, the response will be a unilateral hunt against the responsible party, not consultation. The Slade template applies. She will not tell Clint and she will not tell Kate that she is doing it.

**Leverage.** Threats to Kate would move Bobbi off doctrine faster than threats to almost anyone else, Clint included — because Clint can be assumed to handle himself and Kate is still, in Bobbi's mental schema, in the developmental window where a senior is supposed to be the floor under her.

---

## 4. JESSICA DREW — Peer, Comrade, the Other Survivor of Captivity

**History.** Their friendship predates the Skrull crisis but is forged into something different by it. Both women lost time to Skrull captivity; both came back to a world where their faces had been worn by enemies; both had to rebuild trust with partners and colleagues who had spent years interacting with replacements. Almost no one else in their cohort has this specific data point. Jessica is the only person Bobbi will discuss the captivity with even glancingly, and only obliquely, and only sometimes.

**Dynamic.** A friendship of *parallel privacy*. They will sit in a kitchen drinking coffee for an hour and exchange perhaps eight sentences and consider the visit a success. Jessica reads Bobbi's silences accurately and does not interpret them as withholding from *her*; she understands they are withholding from the air, and that being permitted to share the air is itself the message. Bobbi has noted that Jessica is one of two people in whose physical proximity her shoulders measurably drop — a somatic tell she has caught herself in and not corrected.

**Trust posture.** Information-sharing: high on operational matters, near-total on captivity-adjacent matters (cautious phrasing, no detail), restricted on Clint-related matters where Bobbi feels Jessica's loyalties are not perfectly aligned with hers. Action-sharing: Jessica is one of the few she will call for back-up *before* the situation becomes critical, rather than after. This is significant; Bobbi's default is to call after.

**Failure mode.** The risk is mirror-collapse: in periods when Jessica is herself decompensating from her own trauma load, Bobbi has historically over-extended to support her in ways that drain Bobbi's already-thin reserves, because the alternative — admitting she cannot carry both of them — would require asking for help from a third party. She has not yet built the muscle for that triangulation.

**Leverage.** An adversary who staged a Skrull-style impersonation incident around Jessica would compromise Bobbi's ordinary verification protocols, because the relationship runs partly on a recognition that bypasses ordinary auth steps. She knows this and has built no compensating control.

---

## 5. JAMES "BUCKY" BARNES — Operational Brother, the Quiet One

**History.** Their professional intersection is post-his-rehabilitation, in Secret Avengers-adjacent contexts. The relationship developed without the small talk most relationships require because neither of them does small talk. They worked a series of operations together, found that their tradecraft instincts matched at a level that needed almost no verbal coordination, and gradually developed the kind of partnership that is more comfortable than friendship and less labelled than it.

**Dynamic.** They do not hang out. They do not call each other for non-operational reasons. When they are in the same room they stand near each other, not speaking, and other people in the room interpret this correctly as a closed channel. Bobbi reads Bucky as the only operator in her cohort whose interior trauma load is genuinely comparable to hers and possibly heavier — and unlike everyone else who knows this about him, she does not feel any impulse to fix it. She trusts him to manage his own freight. He returns the courtesy.

**Trust posture.** Operationally: she will take point if he asks her to, will hand him point if he prefers, will follow his read of a room over hers in close-quarters situations because his counter-surveillance instincts are sharper than anyone else she has worked with. Personally: they do not have a personal channel and the absence of one is the relationship's load-bearing feature.

**Failure mode.** If either of them ever needed to ask the other for help with an interior matter, neither knows how the conversation would start. The relationship's architecture does not include that move.

**Leverage.** Very limited from outside. An adversary trying to exploit this bond would need to understand it well enough to know not to try to threaten one through the other in any obvious way — both would simply execute the threatening party without ceremony.

---

## 6. SIMON WILLIAMS — The Friend Who Knew Her Before

**History.** West Coast Avengers period. Simon was the teammate Bobbi found least operationally impressive and most personally bearable, which produced an unexpected friendship. He talked too much, performed his vulnerabilities, processed grief in public — every behavior she finds aversive in herself — and watching him do it without consequence taught her something she has not been willing to fully metabolize.

**Dynamic.** The friendship is intermittent and survives long gaps. When they reconnect after years apart, both default to the cadence they had in the WCA tower: she dry, he expansive, both fond. He is one of perhaps two living people who remember the pre-Slade Bobbi from the inside, which makes him a kind of memorial archive she occasionally consults.

**Trust posture.** She will tell Simon things she will not tell Clint, on the precise grounds that Simon has no operational stake and no romantic stake and therefore receives the information cleanly. She does not tell him everything; she tells him *some* of the Slade interior, which she has told essentially no one else, and she did so once, over a kitchen table, late, after the third drink she does not usually permit herself.

**Failure mode.** His own death-and-return cycles have repeatedly tested whether the friendship survives long discontinuities; so far it has. The risk is not betrayal but attrition — eventually a return where the cadence does not re-establish.

**Leverage.** Limited and indirect. The relationship is too off-grid for most adversaries to model.

---

## 7. STEVEN ROGERS — The Reference Standard

**History.** Cross-paths through Avengers and SHIELD channels over decades. Never a partner, never a confidant; instead a *standard against which she calibrates her ethical instrument*.

**Dynamic.** She respects him in a particular way: not as an inspiration (she is not inspirable in that mode) but as a working example that the integrated moral-tactical operator is possible. When she has to make a hard call she will sometimes briefly run the *Rogers check* — what would he see, what would he say — and then make her own call, which is frequently not the one he would make. The fact that she runs the check is the part that matters; the fact that she overrides it is consistent with her core operational signature.

**Trust posture.** She will follow his lead in joint operations without friction. She will not share interior material with him; he is too institutionally located, and his ethical clarity would, she suspects, make him a poor recipient of her grey-area history. She suspects he would *try* to receive it well, and the trying would hurt.

**Failure mode.** None active. The relationship is well-bounded.

**Leverage.** An adversary who could make her believe Rogers had endorsed a course of action would not get a free pass — she would still verify — but the verification window would be longer than for almost any other source.

---

## 8. NATASHA ROMANOVA — Counterpart, Wary Mirror

**History.** Two women of overlapping but not identical tradecraft generations, both run by male handlers, both with significant trauma loads expressed through tight affect regulation, both with Barton in their relational histories. The intersection should produce either a deep friendship or a careful distance; it has produced the latter.

**Dynamic.** Professional respect at the maximum level — Bobbi considers Natasha possibly the only field operator whose all-around tradecraft exceeds hers and is comfortable saying so. Personally they keep a clean perimeter. The Barton overlap is part of it; more substantially, each correctly recognizes that the other uses many of the same defenses, and being mirrored at that depth is unrestful. They circle, they collaborate cleanly, they do not seek each other out.

**Trust posture.** Operational trust very high. Information trust selective and reciprocal — they trade real intel, neither pads, neither holds back the material the other needs. Personal trust unbuilt by choice, on both sides.

**Failure mode.** If they were ever required by circumstance to depend on each other for emotional survival in a hostage or captivity situation, the dynamic is untested and might produce either a real bond or a sustained mutual freeze. Bobbi privately suspects the latter and has not stress-tested the assumption.

**Leverage.** Almost none. The relationship's deliberate thinness is itself a security feature.

---

## 9. WILMA CALVIN — Origin-Era Asset / Ethical Debt

**History.** The scientist Bobbi was originally sent to surveil and ultimately to protect under the Huntress cover. The operation closed cleanly enough on paper but Bobbi carries a private acknowledgment that the relationship began in deception and that Calvin never received a full debrief on what Bobbi had actually been doing in her lab.

**Dynamic.** Mostly latent. Bobbi has kept loose tabs on Calvin's career across decades — a passive monitoring habit she does not examine — and has twice, unsolicited, intervened to remove threats to Calvin that Calvin never learned about. This is one of the clearest examples in her file of *atonement-without-disclosure*, structurally identical to the Slade concealment but inverted in valence: a unilateral protective decision absorbed silently.

**Trust posture.** N/A in the ordinary sense; the relationship is operationally one-directional.

**Failure mode.** If Calvin ever learned the full history of the original surveillance, Bobbi would receive the judgment without defense, and would not contact Calvin again. She has rehearsed this scenario.

**Leverage.** An adversary who staged a credible threat against Calvin would draw Bobbi off-station within hours.

---

## 10. THE WEST COAST COHORT (Bulk Entry) — Pym, Van Dyne, Hank McCoy-adjacent, the broader rotating roster

**History.** Her formative *team* environment, distinct from her formative *handler* environment under Fury. The WCA period was where she learned the texture of mixed-modality teamwork — the scientist-mystic-strongman-archer ensemble — and where her instinct to operate alone was systematically challenged.

**Dynamic.** Affectionate, dated, occasionally reactivated when veterans of that period cross her path. She holds the cohort in a particular memorial regard because it is the period of her life in which she was *least guarded* and which Slade's intrusion ended. Returning to that emotional baseline is not available to her; the cohort is therefore archived rather than active.

**Trust posture.** Will respond to any of them on an old-friend channel; will not initiate intimate contact; will reliably show up for funerals, retirements, weddings, public reaffiliations.

**Failure mode.** Cumulative attrition of the cohort produces a low-grade grief she does not name and does not budget for.

**Leverage.** Diffuse. Threats against the cohort collectively would mobilize her; threats against individuals would mobilize her at calibrated intensity per individual.

---

## 11. PROTÉGÉS, PLURAL — The Junior Operators She Has Quietly Trained

**History.** Across SHIELD, Avengers training programs, and ad-hoc field assignments, Bobbi has run point on the development of perhaps a dozen junior operators whose names do not appear in any formal mentorship roster. Her preference is for women, for analysts being cross-trained into field work, and for operators whose academic background was overridden by their recruitment — people, in short, structurally similar to her younger self.

**Dynamic.** She instructs by *modelling and correction*, rarely by lecture. Her praise is rare and specific; her criticism is rare and structural. Juniors report that working with her is the hardest and clearest experience of their training and that they understand themselves better afterward. Several have attempted to thank her years later and found her uncomfortable receiving it.

**Trust posture.** She invests real interior energy in these relationships during the training window and then steps back hard once the junior is operational, on the theory that lingering would compromise the junior's autonomy. Several have read this as abandonment; she considers it discipline.

**Failure mode.** A protégée killed in the field on an operation Bobbi authorized or shaped is the single category of loss that has historically come closest to breaking her affect regulation. She has lost two. Neither is discussed.

**Leverage.** A surviving protégée taken hostage or turned would move her further off doctrine than nearly any other vector save Clint and Kate.

---

## 12. THE ABSENCES — Worth Naming

A complete relational map of this subject must note the categories of attachment that are *not present* and whose absence is data.

- **No close civilian friends.** Every sustained adult relationship is with someone inside the operational world. The cover identities she has maintained over decades produced acquaintances, not friendships; she has not permitted civilian intimacy since her graduate-school years.
- **No surviving family of origin in any active capacity.** The biological-family channel is dormant or closed in canon and behaviorally absent in her routines.
- **No therapist, no spiritual director, no equivalent professional confidant.** A figure of her trauma load and tenure operating without any structured interior-disclosure relationship is a significant omission and a primary driver of the unilateral-decision pattern. The closest functional substitute is Jessica Drew, and the substitution is partial.
- **No children, no godchildren formally designated, no chosen-family arrangement of the kind some of her cohort have built.** Kate Bishop is the closest thing in the record to a chosen daughter and the designation is unspoken on both sides.

The shape of these absences is not random. They are the negative space cast by the same structure that produces the unilateral decisions: a person organized around the conviction that interior material is hers to bear and that bearing it is both a competence and a kindness. Every relationship in this section has been shaped, at one boundary or another, by that conviction.

---

*End Section. Cross-reference: Relationships I (Romantic-Primary: Barton); Relationships III (Adversaries & Compromised Bonds); Behavioral Annex C (Unilateral-Decision Pattern).*


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*File continuation. Cross-reference with Relationships I (Kin & Foundational) and II (Operational Peers & Mentees). This section maps the figures who have either tried to destroy the subject, tried to possess her, or done both in alternating sequence. The taxonomy is deliberately blurred: in her file, lover and adversary are not adjacent categories — they overlap, frequently in the same body.*

---

## A. INTIMATES & LOVERS

### A.1 — Clinton Francis Barton ("Hawkeye"). Husband; ex-husband; recurring partner; structural gravity.

**Origin of the bond.** First sustained contact during the Cross Technological Enterprises infiltration arc, when she is still operating as Huntress and he is freelancing post-Avengers. Functional first impression: he is loud, fast, undisciplined, emotionally legible to the point of transparency. She is the inverse on every axis. The attraction is mechanical before it is romantic — she reads him in ninety seconds, he cannot read her at all, and that asymmetry is both the engine and the eventual fault line. They marry within an operationally indefensible timeframe (the Las Vegas marriage in the Gruenwald limited series); the file notes this as the only documented impulsive personal decision in her recorded life. Hypothesis: she married him precisely because the decision was not characteristic — a deliberate violation of her own pattern, an experiment in being someone who *could* do that.

**Dynamic, longitudinally.** Three stable modes, cycled:

1. **Co-operational pair-bonding (West Coast Avengers, early).** They run as a tactical unit; he provides volume and reach, she provides reconnaissance and close-quarters. She is the planner; he is the improviser; the team works because each tolerates the other's primary mode without trying to convert them. Domestic life: she cooks rarely and competently, he cooks often and badly, she does the household administration without comment, he notices late. He talks through every feeling; she absorbs and rarely returns. He experiences this as restful early and starving later.

2. **Rupture (Phantom Rider arc through divorce).** The Slade concealment is not, in her interior accounting, primarily a sexual-assault concealment — it is a *lethal-decision* concealment. She does not believe he can metabolize her having let a man die. She is right that he cannot, and wrong that it was the only path. When he learns, the rupture is total but not loud: he goes quiet in a way she has never seen, and that quiet is the punishment. They separate on stated grounds of irreconcilable approaches to lethal force; the actual ground is breach of disclosure.

3. **Re-entanglement, plural (post-resurrection, post-Skrull, post-everything).** They orbit. They cohabit briefly. They run joint operations (the McCann *Hawkeye & Mockingbird* arc, the WCA Initiative period, the various Avengers crossovers). They sleep together; they separate; neither files a final divorce of the bond itself. The pattern is *return without resolution*. She comes back when she is hurt or when he is; she leaves when proximity demands a level of disclosure she cannot supply.

**Trust register.** Operationally: complete and reciprocal — she will trust him with her exposed back in a firefight at a confidence level she extends to perhaps three other people alive. Emotionally: asymmetric and corroded. He trusts her with everything; she trusts him with what she has pre-classified as releasable.

**Safety register.** He is the person most able to wound her and least likely to try. She is the person most able to wound him and has done so twice — once by the concealment, once by the absences. Neither of them experiences the other as physically unsafe; both experience the other as the locus of the worst pain available to them.

**Failure mode of the bond.** It does not fail by conflict. It fails by her unilateral acts and her withdrawal *into competence* under stress. When she is most strained, she stops talking and starts solving; he reads this as exclusion (correctly) and as rejection (incorrectly), and the gap widens.

**Leverage.** Anyone who can credibly threaten Barton has the only reliable lever on the subject's decision-making. The Phantom Rider knew it instinctively. The Skrull infiltrator weaponized the marriage to deceive him. Future hostile actors will reach for the same handle; it is the cleanest one available.

---

### A.2 — Lance Hunter. Second-tier intimate; lower-stakes coupling; functional rebound architecture.

(Where canon registers him as a romantic partner in the spy-team configurations, the dynamic is markedly different from Barton.) He is, in personality terms, a *Barton analog with British inflection and more institutional fluency* — talkative, emotionally available, slightly chaotic, lower volume. The structural similarity is the diagnostic: she selects, again, the man who will demand more disclosure than she will give. The difference is that with Hunter the stakes are pre-negotiated as lower; both parties know it. She uses the relationship as a controlled study in whether she can do the Barton thing differently this time. The answer is: somewhat. She discloses more, marries less, leaves earlier and cleaner. The relationship's primary function in her file is *practice-without-consequences* — she is learning, late, how to be in something without making it a vow.

**Trust register.** Moderate, professional-leaning. **Safety register.** Higher than with Barton precisely because lower-stakes. **Failure mode.** Eventually he asks for what Barton asked for, and she cannot supply it any more than before, but the breakup does not unmake her. **Leverage.** Minimal — he is not the handle Barton is.

---

### A.3 — Lincoln Slade ("Phantom Rider"). Lover by criminal coercion; victimizer; corpse.

This is filed under "lovers" because canon obliges the bookkeeping; the file insists it is an assault. He was the man who drugged her into compliance, who staged the trappings of a marriage she did not consent to, who deformed her cognition with herbal compounds until consent became a category she could not access. The "relationship" never existed; the violation did.

**Dynamic.** Captor and captive in romantic costume. He believed — and this is important to her interior accounting — that he loved her. The fact that her assailant was sincere in his delusion is part of what makes the memory unmanageable; pure malice would be cleaner. She cannot file him as a monster, only as a man who had constructed a feeling and then used drugs to extract its object.

**Resolution.** When the compounds wore and her clarity returned, she did not save him from the fall. The decision was made in approximately the span of three seconds and has held for the rest of her life. She does not, on reflection, retract it. She also does not present it as righteous. It sits in her ledger as *the thing she did that was hers*.

**Trust register / safety register.** Not applicable; he is the negative pole of both. **Failure mode of the entanglement.** It produced the central concealment of her life and ended her marriage. **Leverage, posthumous.** The Hamilton Slade haunting arc — the brother weaponizing the dead man's ghost against her — demonstrates that the Slade material is *permanent* leverage on her, externally accessible to anyone willing to invoke it. She is hardened against it now but the cost of the hardening is itself a vulnerability.

---

## B. RIVALS

### B.1 — Natasha Romanoff. Professional rival; non-enemy; mirror.

Not an enemy in any operational sense; the two have run joint ops competently across decades. The rivalry is structural and largely silent: they occupy adjacent niches in the same intelligence ecology — superlatively trained female covert operative with scientific/technical fluency and a complicated relationship to a senior Avenger — and the field is not large enough for the comparison not to register. Romanoff is the older, deeper, more compromised version of the role; the subject is the more recently institutional, less morally pre-stained version.

**Dynamic.** Professionally cordial, mildly cool, marked by the kind of compressed verbal economy two people use when each knows the other is reading them at full bandwidth. They do not socialize. They do not confide. They will absolutely cover each other in a hot zone and have done so. There is mutual respect and a refusal of intimacy that is, on both sides, somewhat relieved.

**Failure mode.** A scenario forcing them into prolonged co-leadership without a clear operational hierarchy; both default to command, neither yields gracefully, and the team underneath would experience the friction.

**Leverage.** Each could, in principle, predict the other's tradecraft choices to a dangerous degree. Neither will, absent extraordinary cause.

---

### B.2 — Wilma Calvin / the original CTE operation. Foundational professional adversary; rival as proof-of-concept.

The Calvin operation is where she became the operative the rest of the file describes. Calvin is not personally consequential as an ongoing enemy; she is consequential as the first time the subject ran a multi-month deep cover under a fabricated scientific identity and held it. The rivalry was asymmetric — Calvin never knew she was being run on — but the subject's interior register treats Calvin as the first real *opponent* and the operation as her professional confirmation. Subsequent behavior under cover descends from this template: she over-prepares the cover identity to the point that it becomes a usable secondary self, and she has difficulty fully disassembling it after extraction.

---

### B.3 — Internal rivalry: the impersonator. The Skrull who wore her face.

Filed here because the subject's relationship to this entity is structurally a rivalry — the Skrull was, by every external measure, *better at being her than she was*, for years. The infiltrator successfully ran her marriage, her professional life, her institutional reputation, without detection by people who had known her for decades. The interior implication, which she has never spoken aloud and which the file infers from behavioral residue, is devastating: if a stranger could pass as her seamlessly, what does that say about how legible *she* was to the people she loved? The answer she has arrived at is *not very*, and the answer reinforces the very compartmentalization that produced the legibility gap in the first place. The Skrull is dead; the rivalry, in her head, is permanent.

---

## C. ENEMIES

### C.1 — Mephisto. Cosmological enemy; the agent of her death.

Functionally not a personal antagonist — she did not warrant his attention; she stepped in front of an attack meant for Barton. He is filed nevertheless because the encounter terminated her life in its prior iteration and the death has organized everything she has done since. **Dynamic.** Asymmetric to the point of absurdity; she is to him a footnote. He is to her the proof that sacrificial substitution was inside her behavioral repertoire — she did not deliberate, she stepped. The post-resurrection Bobbi has had to integrate the data point that *her body chose Barton without consulting her*, which is both confirming (the bond is what she thought it was) and disquieting (her vaunted deliberation is overrideable at the limit). **Leverage.** None he would bother to exercise. **Threat profile.** She does not plan against him; she plans against being in rooms where he is plausible.

---

### C.2 — Hamilton Slade. Vengeance-driven secondary antagonist; ghost-vector for Lincoln.

Lincoln's brother. Inherited the Phantom Rider mantle and the family grievance; pursued her with the explicit intent of forcing her to relive the killing under supernatural duress. Operationally a mid-tier threat; psychologically a precision weapon, because he attacks at the one site she cannot fully defend. Her handling of him is informative: she does not destabilize, she does not apologize, she does not negotiate. She wins the encounters and refuses the catharsis Hamilton is demanding from her. This is consistent with her general pattern — she will not stage feelings for an audience, even an audience entitled to them.

**Failure mode.** A scenario in which Hamilton, or an heir of his grievance, captures Barton and stages a re-enactment requiring her to choose between confession and Barton's life. She would confess. She would also kill the captor. Both, in order.

---

### C.3 — Skrull captors (collective). Captivity-trauma origin; impersonal apparatus.

She does not know most of their names. The file treats them as a *condition* she survived rather than as individuals she opposes. Operationally: years of interrogation, debriefing, sensory manipulation, and the constant epistemic injury of watching herself be studied for the purpose of replication. **Dynamic.** Total power asymmetry; she developed, in captivity, the deep-form compartmentalization that distinguishes her post-return cognition from her pre-capture cognition. The defense, in other words, was *built in their facility*. She walked out of captivity with their tools welded into her. **Leverage, residual.** Any species-level Skrull resurgence will reach for her as a person of known compliance-profile; she knows this and treats every novel shapeshifter encounter as a Skrull-priors event until proven otherwise.

---

### C.4 — AIM, HYDRA, the standing roster of intelligence-grade adversaries.

Generic, in the sense that any senior SHIELD-tier operative accumulates the same enemies list. She has burned cells, killed mid-level operatives, extracted assets, and turned defectors across the full canonical run. The file does not list these individually because none of them have penetrated her interior life. She regards them as workload. Two specific patterns worth noting:

- She prefers *non-lethal* resolution where tactically possible — a preference that postdates the Slade event and is, on the evidence, partly atonement-coded. She will kill cleanly when required; she will not kill *to make a point*.
- She maintains, in violation of SHIELD policy, private files on certain HYDRA mid-tier operatives — personal-history dossiers, family connections, vulnerabilities — that she has never operationalized. The hypothesis: she keeps them as *reserve leverage* against the day institutional protection of those targets fails. This is consistent with her structural distrust of institutions and her insistence on personal-actor backstops.

---

### C.5 — Institutional adversaries: SHIELD leadership when SHIELD is wrong.

Not enemies in the criminal sense; opposing-interest parties when the institution's calculus diverges from her own. She has lied to Fury, to Hill, to Coulson, to successor directors, when she has judged the institutional decision wrong. She has not been caught at most of these lies. The file's standing assessment: she will continue to do this, the rate will increase with seniority, and the day she is asked to lie to Barton about an institutional order she has refused to follow is the day a structurally significant rupture will occur unless she has by then learned to disclose. Current probability of that learning: low but non-zero, rising slowly with age.

---

## D. SUMMARY OF LEVERAGE LANDSCAPE

The subject's enemies list is, by intelligence-community standards, *modest in volume and concentrated in depth*. She is not a person with a thousand grievances arrayed against her; she is a person with perhaps a dozen vectors of true exposure, of which three matter:

1. **Barton.** The only reliable behavioral lever. Any actor who controls him controls her decision tree for the duration.
2. **The Slade material.** Permanent, externally invocable, defended but not neutralized.
3. **Identity / impersonation attacks.** Post-Skrull, any operation that calls her authenticity into question forces her into a defensive posture she has not fully rehearsed out of.

Conversely, her lovers list is *small, structurally repetitive, and revealing*: she selects, with one assault-exception that does not count as selection, men who demand more emotional disclosure than she will provide, and she leaves when the demand becomes load-bearing. The pattern is not a failure to learn; it is a deliberate, semi-conscious test, run repeatedly, of whether she has yet become the kind of person who can stay. The current data does not support that she has. The file leaves the question open.

*— End Relationships III. Continue to Relationships IV (Institutional & Operational Affiliations).*


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: BOBBI MORSE
## Section 6 — Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

---

### 6.1 Baseline Physiology (Post-Augmentation)

Bobbi Morse possesses no mutation, no extra-dimensional birthright, no symbiote, no inherited gift. Every capacity in her file is *built* — by training, by credential, by tradecraft repetition, or by a single non-consensual medical event whose effects she has chosen to inventory, weaponize, and never quite trust.

**Pre-augmentation baseline** (the Englehart/Trimpe through Gruenwald era): an Olympic-tier athlete's somatic envelope. Sprint capacity in the high-end human range, vertical leap and grip strength consistent with elite gymnastic and parkour-trained operatives, vO2 max in the upper percentile for her body mass. Reflex latency measurably faster than mean SHIELD field-agent baseline (her qualifying scores are repeatedly invoked as among the best of her intake). Pain tolerance trained, not innate — she absorbs strikes she should not absorb because she has been conditioned to keep working through them, not because nerve transmission is dulled.

**Post-augmentation profile** (post-*Hawkeye & Mockingbird* / *New Avengers* era): the combined Super-Soldier Serum variant and Infinity Formula infusion produced:

- **Strength**: ceiling raised from "peak human female" to roughly the lower band of enhanced — she presses meaningfully above her old one-rep max, but she is not Cap, not Jessica Drew on a good day, not in the Luke Cage tier. She is, specifically, *able to hit harder than her opponent expects from her frame*, which is the operationally useful zone.
- **Durability**: subdermal resilience and connective-tissue integrity improved. Strikes that would have broken her ribs now bruise them. Concussive thresholds raised but not eliminated.
- **Healing**: lacerations and fractures resolve in days rather than weeks. She does not regenerate tissue (no severed limb returns); she repairs at an accelerated rate from a non-destroyed substrate.
- **Aging**: arrested or radically decelerated. She presents in her mid-thirties across decades of publication time. She does not discuss this. Ever. The silence is the data: the Infinity Formula carries a Fury-shaped historical association she has not invited into her self-concept.
- **Disease resistance**: substantially elevated. She does not catch what is going around the safehouse.

The *psychological* fact of the augmentation matters more than the somatic one: she did not choose it, was unconscious when it was administered, and lives in a body whose ceiling was set by someone else's emergency triage. She trains as if she still has the old body, and treats the additional margin as a tactical surprise to be deployed, not a baseline to be relied on. This is consistent with her broader pattern of refusing to accept gifts whose price she did not negotiate.

---

### 6.2 Hand-to-Hand Combat

She is a *composite* martial artist in the SHIELD-Romanoff-Barton tradition: no single school, every school as a vocabulary. Documented influences across her training arc include collegiate gymnastics, Western boxing fundamentals, judo and aikido throws, escrima stickwork (the through-line into the battle staves), Krav Maga close-quarters work, and the SHIELD finishing-school synthesis that Fury's program imposed on all of it. She is not a stylist; she is an *outcome operator*. She picks the technique that ends the encounter in the fewest tempos with the least signature.

**Signature application** — the **dual battle staves**. Telescoping, often electrified or kinetically charged depending on the era's tech budget, deployed from compact baton form by a sharp wrist flick that has become a personal tic (she does it absently while thinking, snapping a closed baton open and shut as a kind of fidget — see §7 if appended). Her staff work is *legwork-forward*: she fights from her hips and ankles, the staves are the punctuation. Range advantage against unenhanced opponents is decisive — she keeps the engagement at two-stave-lengths until she decides to close. When she closes, she closes *inside* the opponent's reach, not at it, using the staff hafts as leverage points for throws and joint locks rather than as striking surfaces.

**Limits**: she will lose a straight-line strength contest with any genuinely super-strong opponent and knows it. Her solution is to never let the engagement be a strength contest. She fights *angles*, fights *terrain*, fights *attention*. Against opponents whose perception or speed exceeds hers (Quicksilver-tier, certain telepaths who read intent) her tradecraft collapses into reactive defense and she has historically been forced to disengage rather than win.

**Sparring tells**: she favors her left lead despite right-hand dominance — a deliberate trained inversion from her undercover days, when matching expected handedness in surveillance footage was contraindicated. She breathes through her nose in combat, exhaling on impact in measured counts. She does not vocalize. The absence of vocalization is itself unusual at her tier and is a small signature that has been used to identify her on grainy security feeds.

---

### 6.3 Espionage Tradecraft

This is her actual primary power.

**Cover identity construction**: she can build and sustain a cover for months to years. The Wilma Calvin operation (her introductory deep-cover work) ran long enough that her "Bobbi the consulting biologist" cover was not a cover at all — it was *her*, with a different reporting line. Her tradecraft principle is that the best cover is one in which 95% of the surface is true. She lies in the load-bearing 5% and lets the rest of her actual life carry the weight. This is also, not coincidentally, her interpersonal style.

**Surveillance and counter-surveillance**: she runs SDRs (surveillance detection routes) reflexively even off-mission — she will alter her path to the grocery, change subway cars one stop early, double back through a department store. She has a documented preference for retail environments with multiple egresses and mirrored surfaces. She memorizes the faces in any room she enters within the first ninety seconds and can recall them days later; this is trained eidetic recall on specific stimulus classes (faces, license plates, hands), not general eidetic memory.

**Elicitation**: she can run a conversation that extracts an asset's operational details without the asset registering the interview. Her technique is heavy on *strategic self-disclosure* — she trades small, calibrated truths about herself to lower a subject's guard. The disclosures are real. They are not, however, the disclosures that matter to her, which is what makes the technique sustainable: she is spending the cheap currency.

**Infiltration**: lockpicking (mechanical and electronic at field-agent grade, not Widow-tier), social engineering, document forgery sufficient for tactical use (she relies on SHIELD/agency document shops for anything that needs to survive a serious check), HUMINT cultivation, dead-drop and brush-pass mechanics ingrained to the point of unconscious execution.

**Interrogation**: she runs rapport-based interrogations almost exclusively. She does not torture. This is ethical but also operational — she believes (correctly, by the empirical literature) that information from coercion is unreliable, and she has the patience to win the slower way. Her interrogation room voice drops about a third of a semitone and slows by perhaps fifteen percent; subjects often describe feeling listened-to in retrospect and only later realize they were processed.

**Counter-interrogation (her own)**: this is where the Skrull captivity left its mark. Pre-captivity she could be expected to hold cover under standard hostile interrogation indefinitely. Post-captivity her resistance is no less effective but its character changed — she now holds by *dissociating from the speaker* rather than by managing the speaker. She goes interior. Debriefers have noted she becomes harder to read on her own side as well after such episodes.

---

### 6.4 Scientific & Technical Competencies

The dossier must be exhaustive here because the publication record consistently underuses what is, on paper, her highest-credentialed capacity.

**Biology** — her doctorate (or in some renderings, doctorates). Specializations across the canon include molecular biology, evolutionary biology, and biochemistry. Operationally relevant subsets: toxicology (she identifies neurotoxins by symptom presentation in the field), forensic biology (blood spatter, tissue ID), and bio-defense (pathogen handling protocols, BSL-4 procedures). She has authored at least one published paper of canonical reference in her pre-SHIELD academic phase, which functions as a verifiable cover credential.

**Chemistry** — sufficient to synthesize field-expedient compounds: improvised explosives, smoke and obscurant mixtures, certain sedatives and stimulants. She maintains a working knowledge of pharmacology adequate to dose unfamiliar bodies (including non-human physiologies, which she has had to do more than once).

**Engineering / armorer skills** — she maintains, modifies, and field-repairs her own staves. She is conversant with SHIELD-issue firearms across generations but is not a gun-first operator; her preference for staves is partly tactical (non-lethal options, reach, multi-use as climbing and leverage tools) and partly somatic (she does not like the *report* of firearms — see Skrull captivity sensory residue).

**Computers / SIGINT** — competent but not specialist. She runs encrypted comms, can perform basic network intrusion against soft targets, knows when to call someone better. She is not Bobbi-Drew or Daisy Johnson at a terminal and does not pretend otherwise.

**Languages** — Russian (operationally fluent), Mandarin (working), Japanese (working), French (conversational), several others at the cover-identity-survival level (enough to order a meal, ask directions, fail a native test gracefully). Accent control is excellent in Russian, adequate elsewhere.

**The under-use phenomenon**: the canon repeatedly puts her in a costume when her PhD would be the right instrument. She has internalized this. In her own self-narration she defaults to "agent" rather than "scientist," which is itself a defensive choice — the scientist identity is the one she would lose more if it were threatened, so she leads with the one she can replace.

---

### 6.5 Growth Curve Over Publication Time

- **1971–1980 (Astonishing Tales / Marvel Team-Up era)**: scientist-foregrounded, espionage-backgrounded. Combat capacity present but unrefined relative to later. The "Huntress" identity reads as a competent-but-junior field operative.
- **1980–1989 (Hawkeye limited / WCA)**: full operational maturity. Staff work codified. Combat tempo and tactical confidence at career peak. Partnership tactics with Clint developed into a documented two-operator doctrine (he provides ranged interdiction, she provides close engagement and battlefield intelligence — a specialization she has retained even when partnered with others).
- **1989–1993 (late WCA to death)**: marginal somatic gains, marked psychological compression after the Slade arc. Performance unaffected on metrics; affect noticeably more sealed.
- **2008–present (post-Skrull return)**: physical augmentation raises her ceiling; experience and caution raise her floor. She fights *smaller* than she used to — fewer flourishes, less acrobatic display, more economy. The change is consistent with the captivity history (reduced tolerance for performative motion, preference for minimal signature). Her tactical creativity actually expands — she improvises more, telegraphs less, and shows a marked uptick in willingness to use environmental hazards against opponents (the Cain run displays this repeatedly).

---

### 6.6 Signature Applications

A short catalog of the *moves* her file would tag for pattern recognition:

- **The staff-spin entry**: she enters a room with one staff already deployed at her side in a low loose grip, the other still collapsed in her off hand. The deployed staff is the decoy; the collapsed one is what hits you.
- **The conversational disarm**: she defuses a tense standoff by asking a precise, slightly inappropriate question that requires the subject to think for a half-second. In that half-second she has closed distance or rerouted the encounter.
- **The medical takedown**: she ends fights by targeting specific anatomical structures (brachial plexus, common peroneal nerve at the lateral knee, the vagus response at the carotid sinus) with the staff tip. This is *biologist's combat* — she knows exactly what she is hitting.
- **The clean exit**: she leaves operational sites without trail. Her exfil discipline is among the best in her cohort; she is rarely the operator whose departure is caught on camera.

---

### 6.7 Limits — A Hard Inventory

1. **Strength ceiling**: enhanced but not super-strong by the standards of her usual opposition. Loses contests of raw force.
2. **Speed ceiling**: enhanced reaction time, not enhanced movement speed. Outpaced by speedsters and by certain trained-reflex enhanced opponents.
3. **No ranged power**: no projectile capability beyond weapons she is carrying. If disarmed at distance from a foe with ranged offense, she is in trouble.
4. **No psionic defense beyond training**: she meditates, she compartmentalizes, but a sufficient telepath reads her.
5. **No regeneration of lost tissue**: enhanced healing repairs, does not replace.
6. **Sensory-overload vulnerability**: post-Skrull, sustained high-decibel environments and certain shifting-light conditions produce measurable performance degradation. She has never reported this.
7. **Trust-network dependency**: her tradecraft assumes she will compartmentalize information from her own allies. When the situation requires *coordinated* transparency she is the bottleneck.
8. **Recovery-from-care difficulty**: she performs worse, not better, when being protected. Allies who try to shield her destabilize her tactical model.

---

### 6.8 The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

Every one of her capabilities maps cleanly onto a wound, and reading the capability set as a symptom inventory is the analytically honest move.

- **The doctorate** is a competence-fortress against a self-concept that does not trust *being* and only trusts *doing*. She accumulates credentials the way another trauma profile would accumulate weapons.
- **The tradecraft of compartmentalization** is C-PTSD's signature defense raised to professional grade and remunerated. She was paid for what the trauma was already going to make her do.
- **The staves** — paired, non-lethal-capable, requiring two hands to deploy fully — are a weapon system that *occupies* both of her hands. She is never in a posture of open-handed approach. The somatic vocabulary of her combat style is the somatic vocabulary of her intimacy style: armed, balanced, at measured distance, ready to disengage.
- **The rapport-based interrogation skill** is the *positive expression* of the same capacity that, turned inward, becomes her elicitation of partners — calibrated self-disclosure spent to extract without spending what matters.
- **The accelerated healing and arrested aging** are gifts she did not choose, administered while she was unconscious, that she will use and will not discuss. They are the somatic restatement of the Slade incident and the Phantom Rider drugging: *her body keeps being acted on without her consent, and she keeps integrating the consequence in private*.
- **The exfil discipline** — leaving no trail — is the operational form of her relational pattern. She does not stay. She does not leave evidence she was there. She is *very* good at this, and the goodness is the problem.
- **The refusal to vocalize in combat** is the same silence as the Slade concealment. She does not narrate her violence; she does not narrate her decisions; the noise she does not make is the through-line of the file.

The summary statement her file should carry, operationally: **Bobbi Morse's powers are a faithful externalization of her psychological architecture. She is exactly as dangerous as her defenses are mature, and exactly as vulnerable as those defenses are necessary.** A handler reading only her capability sheet will deploy her brilliantly and lose her quietly. A handler reading this section understands that her competence and her wound are the same instrument held at different angles, and that asking her to set down the instrument is asking her to set down the self she built to survive the things she did not choose.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT: BOBBI MORSE

*UATU Dossier, Section 6 of 14. Compiled from longitudinal observation across the entire published record (1971–present). This section catalogues HOW the subject operates: the granular mechanics of her decision loop, her tradecraft inventory, her infrastructure, her financial substrate, her movement patterns, and the micro-tells by which a sufficiently attentive observer can read her.*

---

## 6.1 Decision Architecture

Morse's decision-making is best modeled as a **two-track parallel process** running continuously, with a third arbitration track that resolves conflicts between them. Track A is the *scientific-hypothetical* engine: observe, hypothesize, design minimal test, update prior, iterate. Track B is the *operational-tradecraft* engine: threat-map, asset-map, exit-map, contingency-map, executable plan. The arbitration layer is the layer that produces her most consequential — and most isolating — behavior: the moment she silently determines whose interests will be sacrificed, and how much she will say about it.

The decision loop is fast — observably faster than her peers in field footage — but it is **not impulsive**. What appears to teammates as a snap call is the visible output of a process that has been running pre-consciously for whatever interval the situation has offered. She does not improvise; she *pre-computes* and then selects from a menu she has already built. This is why her unilateral acts (the Slade non-rescue being the archetype) have the texture of decisions she made calmly some time before the moment they were enacted.

**Cost-distribution heuristic**. When a problem entails an irreducible cost, her default allocation is: *self first, mission second, attachments shielded last*. She does not run a utilitarian calculus that would balance these; she runs a deontological one in which her own absorption of the cost is treated as axiomatic. The Slade concealment from Clint is exactly this rule operating on its second clause — having absorbed the act, she then shielded the attachment from the knowledge of it, on the grounds that the knowledge was *her* cost to carry, not his. This is the rule, restated: *what I did, I bear; what I bore, I do not transfer*.

**Information thresholds**. She will act on lower-quality intelligence than most peers when the downside is borne by her, and demand higher-quality intelligence than most peers when the downside is borne by a partner. Operationally this manifests as a willingness to walk into a building on a hunch when she is alone, and an obstructive insistence on confirmation when Clint or a junior asset is in play.

**Tempo control**. Her preferred operational tempo is *slow-then-instantaneous*: extended reconnaissance and assessment, then sudden full-commit action. She is markedly worse — and knows it — at sustained mid-tempo brawls where decisions must be remade every second and emotional escalation is unavoidable. She structures her engagements to avoid this regime.

---

## 6.2 Pre-Operational Routine

The pre-op signature is one of the most stable behavioral patterns in the record across forty-plus years of published material and across multiple authorial hands — meaning it is character-deep, not stylistic.

- **Wardrobe ritual**. Layered: base compression layer, mid-layer with concealed pockets, outer layer disposable. She dresses *outward* (skin to street), but breaks down the kit *inward* (weapons checked first, comms last). Battons are the *last* item secured before the door — a tell, because once they are on her thighs she is no longer in planning mode and treats interruption as hostile noise.
- **Hair**. Tightly bound for any engagement she expects to enter physically; loose or half-bound when she expects the operation to remain in surveillance/social-engineering phase. An observer who tracks her hair across a 24-hour cycle can map her threat assessment of the next eight hours.
- **Pre-mission meal**. Light, high-protein, eaten standing. She does not sit to eat before a job. This is not superstition; it is a refusal to enter a parasympathetic state.
- **Comms check**. Three-stage: hardware, channel, *call-and-response phrase with the partner*. The phrase changes per op; she will not deploy without it. With Clint she has, across multiple eras, used a private response set drawn from in-jokes — observable in the McCann run — that doubles as a duress code.
- **Solitary minute**. There is, repeatedly across the record, a closed-eye breath sequence she takes immediately before insertion. Four counts in, six counts out, three to five cycles. It is not meditation; it is parasympathetic gating before the sympathetic spike.

---

## 6.3 Tradecraft Inventory

### Physical Tradecraft

- **Movement**: gymnastic baseline (collegiate-grade tumbling overlaid with SHIELD CQB). She moves on the *outside* of any corridor, hugs the long axis of a room, and enters doorways at the hinge side. In a stairwell she takes the inside spiral. These are not stylistic choices; they are the SHIELD entry curriculum executed without thinking about it, which means she does them when injured, drunk (rarely), or distracted.
- **The battlestaves**: her signature weapon platform. The published record shows extraordinary technical range — telescoping, electrified, capable of being joined into a bo, of firing concussive blasts, of acting as grapple anchors. Her grip default is *reverse-grip dominant hand, forward-grip off hand*, which is the grip optimized for *blocking-then-counter* rather than *initiating*. This is diagnostic: she is a counterpuncher by temperament. She closes distance reactively and dominates middle range; she is less comfortable at extreme close range (clinch) and at extreme distance (firearms-primary), though competent in both.
- **Firearms**: trained to SHIELD standard. She carries when the mission profile requires it, prefers not to. The preference is not squeamishness — it is a tradecraft view that firearms commit one to a particular escalation curve that staves do not.
- **Falls and exits**: she will go through a window before she goes through a door she did not enter by. Roof-to-roof preferred over street-level exfil.

### Cognitive / Scientific Tradecraft

- **Field biology and chemistry**: she will run improvised assays in the field with whatever is to hand. The PhD is not decorative; in any operation involving biological agents, narcotics, or unidentified compounds, she is the asset who will identify the substance before evac. She talks herself through the procedure aloud — a teaching-cadence holdover from lab work — which is one of the few times her interior monologue becomes externally audible.
- **Forensic reconstruction**: high competence. She will reconstruct a fight from blood spatter, scuff patterns, and shell casings rather than asking the witness. Distrusts witness testimony as a class.

### Social Engineering

- **Legend discipline**: extreme.
